## Register-MMA contracts

- `mma_m16n8k128_s32_b1_and_popc` takes fragments in C, A, B order, performs AND, population count, and accumulate, and lowers to one convergent, register-only `mma.sync.aligned.m16n8k128.row.col.s32.b1.b1.s32.and.popc` instruction. Every non-exited warp lane must execute the same instruction and qualifiers. Integer overflow is wrapping; runtime validation is not executed on a GPU.
- `mma_m16n8k128_s32_b1_xor_popc` takes fragments in C, A, B order, performs XOR, population count, and accumulate, and lowers to one convergent, register-only `mma.sync.aligned.m16n8k128.row.col.s32.b1.b1.s32.xor.popc` instruction. Every non-exited warp lane must execute the same instruction and qualifiers. Integer overflow is wrapping; runtime validation is not executed on a GPU.
- `mma_m16n8k16_f32_bf16` takes fragments in C, A, B order, performs multiply-accumulate, and lowers to one convergent, register-only `mma.sync.aligned.m16n8k16.row.col.f32.bf16.bf16.f32` instruction. Every non-exited warp lane must execute the same instruction and qualifiers. Integer overflow is not applicable; runtime validation is not executed on a GPU.
- `mma_m16n8k16_f32_f16` takes fragments in C, A, B order, performs multiply-accumulate, and lowers to one convergent, register-only `mma.sync.aligned.m16n8k16.row.col.f32.f16.f16.f32` instruction. Every non-exited warp lane must execute the same instruction and qualifiers. Integer overflow is not applicable; runtime validation is not executed on a GPU.
- `mma_m16n8k16_s32_s8` takes fragments in C, A, B order, performs multiply-accumulate, and lowers to one convergent, register-only `mma.sync.aligned.m16n8k16.row.col.s32.s8.s8.s32` instruction. Every non-exited warp lane must execute the same instruction and qualifiers. Integer overflow is wrapping; runtime validation is not executed on a GPU.
- `mma_m16n8k16_s32_s8_satfinite` takes fragments in C, A, B order, performs multiply-accumulate, and lowers to one convergent, register-only `mma.sync.aligned.m16n8k16.row.col.satfinite.s32.s8.s8.s32` instruction. Every non-exited warp lane must execute the same instruction and qualifiers. Integer overflow is finite saturation; runtime validation is not executed on a GPU.
- `mma_m16n8k16_s32_s8_u8` takes fragments in C, A, B order, performs multiply-accumulate, and lowers to one convergent, register-only `mma.sync.aligned.m16n8k16.row.col.s32.s8.u8.s32` instruction. - `mma_m16n8k16_s32_s8_u8_satfinite` takes fragments in C, A, B order, performs multiply-accumulate, and lowers to one convergent, register-only `mma.sync.aligned.m16n8k16.row.col.satfinite.s32.s8.u8.s32` instruction. ## Sparse-MMA contracts

Its LLVM source record uses A, B, C, metadata, selector order. The selector must be the compile-time constant `0`. Every non-exited warp lane must execute the same instruction and qualifiers. Integer overflow is finite saturation; runtime validation is not executed on a GPU.
- `mma_sp_ordered_metadata_m16n8k64_s32_u4_satfinite` takes fragments in C, A, B, metadata, selector order and lowers to one convergent, register-only `mma.sp::ordered_metadata.sync.aligned.m16n8k64.row.col.satfinite.s32.u4.u4.s32` instruction. Its LLVM source record uses A, B, C, metadata, selector order. The selector must be the compile-time constant `0` or `1`. Every non-exited warp lane must execute the same instruction and qualifiers. Every 4-bit metadata group must be `0x4`, `0x8`, `0x9`, `0xc`, `0xd`, or `0xe`; any other value is undefined behavior. Integer overflow is finite saturation; runtime validation is not executed on a GPU.
- `mma_sp_ordered_metadata_m16n8k64_s32_u8` takes fragments in C, A, B, metadata, selector order and lowers to one convergent, register-only `mma.sp::ordered_metadata.sync.aligned.m16n8k64.row.col.s32.u8.u8.s32` instruction. Its LLVM source record uses A, B, C, metadata, selector order. The selector must be the compile-time constant `0`. Every non-exited warp lane must execute the same instruction and qualifiers. Every 4-bit metadata group must be `0x4`, `0x8`, `0x9`, `0xc`, `0xd`, or `0xe`; any other value is undefined behavior. Integer overflow is wrapping; runtime validation is not executed on a GPU.
- `mma_sp_ordered_metadata_m16n8k64_s32_u8_s8` takes fragments in C, A, B, metadata, selector order and lowers to one convergent, register-only `mma.sp::ordered_metadata.sync.aligned.m16n8k64.row.col.s32.u8.s8.s32` instruction. Every 4-bit metadata group must be `0x4`, `0x8`, `0x9`, `0xc`, `0xd`, or `0xe`; any other value is undefined behavior. Integer overflow is wrapping; runtime validation is not executed on a GPU.
- `mma_sp_ordered_metadata_m16n8k64_s32_u8_s8_satfinite` takes fragments in C, A, B, metadata, selector order and lowers to one convergent, register-only `mma.sp::ordered_metadata.sync.aligned.m16n8k64.row.col.satfinite.s32.u8.s8.s32` instruction. ## Packed-atomic contracts

- `packed_atomic_add_bf16x2` (`bf16x2`): the native PTX instruction starts at `sm_90`; cuda-oxide admits it from sm_90+. Omitted `.sem` / `.scope` mean relaxed GPU scope. Each 16-bit element rounds to nearest-even and `.noftz` preserves subnormal inputs and results. The elements are atomic independently, so the returned `u32` contains old per-element values that may not form one coherent pair. The pointer must address four writable, four-byte-aligned global bytes; do not mix whole-word or non-atomic overlapping access, and every racing atomic must use a mutually inclusive scope.
- `packed_atomic_add_f16x2` (`f16x2`): the native PTX instruction starts at `sm_60`; cuda-oxide admits it from sm_70+. Omitted `.sem` / `.scope` mean relaxed GPU scope. Each 16-bit element rounds to nearest-even and `.noftz` preserves subnormal inputs and results. The elements are atomic independently, so the returned `u32` contains old per-element values that may not form one coherent pair. The pointer must address four writable, four-byte-aligned global bytes; do not mix whole-word or non-atomic overlapping access, and every racing atomic must use a mutually inclusive scope.

## Redux contracts

- `redux_sync_add`: raw and dialect operands are `[member_mask, value]`, adapted to LLVM `(value, membermask)`. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same instruction with the same qualifiers and mask.
- `redux_sync_and`: raw and dialect operands are `[member_mask, value]`, adapted to LLVM `(value, membermask)`. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same instruction with the same qualifiers and mask.
- `redux_sync_max_i32`: raw and dialect operands are `[member_mask, value]`, adapted to LLVM `(value, membermask)`. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same instruction with the same qualifiers and mask.
- `redux_sync_max_u32`: raw and dialect operands are `[member_mask, value]`, adapted to LLVM `(value, membermask)`. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same instruction with the same qualifiers and mask.
- `redux_sync_min_i32`: raw and dialect operands are `[member_mask, value]`, adapted to LLVM `(value, membermask)`. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same instruction with the same qualifiers and mask.
- `redux_sync_min_u32`: raw and dialect operands are `[member_mask, value]`, adapted to LLVM `(value, membermask)`. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same instruction with the same qualifiers and mask.
- `redux_sync_or`: raw and dialect operands are `[member_mask, value]`, adapted to LLVM `(value, membermask)`. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same instruction with the same qualifiers and mask.
- `redux_sync_xor`: raw and dialect operands are `[member_mask, value]`, adapted to LLVM `(value, membermask)`. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same instruction with the same qualifiers and mask.

## Packed-ALU contracts

- `abs_bf16x2` carries one packed `bf16x2` value in a `u32` and lowers to one pure `abs.bf16x2` instruction. The native instruction starts at PTX 7.0 / `sm_80`; cuda-oxide admits it from sm_80+. Backend profile floors: LLVM-NVPTX PTX 7.0 on sm_80+; libNVVM PTX 7.0 on sm_80+.
- `abs_f16x2` carries one packed `f16x2` value in a `u32` and lowers to one pure `abs.f16x2` instruction. The native instruction starts at PTX 6.5 / `sm_53`; cuda-oxide admits it from sm_70+. Backend profile floors: LLVM-NVPTX PTX 6.5 on sm_70+; libNVVM PTX 6.5 on sm_75+.
- `add_bf16x2` carries one packed `bf16x2` value in a `u32` and lowers to one pure `add.rn.bf16x2` instruction. The native instruction starts at PTX 7.8 / `sm_90`; cuda-oxide admits it from sm_90+. Backend profile floors: LLVM-NVPTX PTX 7.8 on sm_90+; libNVVM PTX 7.8 on sm_90+.

- `fma_relu_bf16x2` carries one packed `bf16x2` value in a `u32` and lowers to one pure `fma.rn.relu.bf16x2` instruction. The native instruction starts at PTX 7.0 / `sm_80`; cuda-oxide admits it from sm_80+. Backend profile floors: LLVM-NVPTX PTX 7.0 on sm_80+; libNVVM PTX 7.0 on sm_80+.

## Packed-conversion contract

- `cvt_f16x2_f32` converts two `f32` inputs to packed `f16x2` using nearest-even rounding without saturation. It lowers to pure `cvt.rn.f16x2.f32` inline PTX. The first input becomes the low lane and the second becomes the high lane, so PTX prints the inputs in reverse order.
- `cvt_f32x2_bf16x2` converts two `f32` inputs to packed `bf16x2` using nearest-even rounding without saturation. It lowers to pure `cvt.rn.bf16x2.f32` inline PTX. The first input becomes the low lane and the second becomes the high lane, so PTX prints the inputs in reverse order.
- `cvt_rn_relu_bf16x2_f32` converts two `f32` inputs to packed `bf16x2` using nearest-even rounding with ReLU. It lowers to pure `cvt.rn.relu.bf16x2.f32` inline PTX. The first input becomes the low lane and the second becomes the high lane, so PTX prints the inputs in reverse order.
- `cvt_rn_relu_f16x2_f32` converts two `f32` inputs to packed `f16x2` using nearest-even rounding with ReLU. It lowers to pure `cvt.rn.relu.f16x2.f32` inline PTX. The first input becomes the low lane and the second becomes the high lane, so PTX prints the inputs in reverse order.
- `cvt_rz_bf16x2_f32` converts two `f32` inputs to packed `bf16x2` using toward-zero rounding without saturation. It lowers to pure `cvt.rz.bf16x2.f32` inline PTX. The first input becomes the low lane and the second becomes the high lane, so PTX prints the inputs in reverse order.
- `cvt_rz_f16x2_f32` converts two `f32` inputs to packed `f16x2` using toward-zero rounding without saturation. It lowers to pure `cvt.rz.f16x2.f32` inline PTX. The first input becomes the low lane and the second becomes the high lane, so PTX prints the inputs in reverse order.

## Warp vote contracts

- `all_sync` keeps raw and dialect operands in `[member_mask, predicate]` order. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `vote.sync` instruction with the same qualifiers and mask. On `sm_6x` and earlier, all named lanes must execute in convergence and no unnamed lane may be active. Both immediate and register member masks are admitted.
- `any_sync` keeps raw and dialect operands in `[member_mask, predicate]` order. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `vote.sync` instruction with the same qualifiers and mask. On `sm_6x` and earlier, all named lanes must execute in convergence and no unnamed lane may be active. Both immediate and register member masks are admitted.
- `ballot_sync` keeps raw and dialect operands in `[member_mask, predicate]` order. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `vote.sync` instruction with the same qualifiers and mask. On `sm_6x` and earlier, all named lanes must execute in convergence and no unnamed lane may be active. Both immediate and register member masks are admitted.
- `uni_sync` keeps raw and dialect operands in `[member_mask, predicate]` order. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `vote.sync` instruction with the same qualifiers and mask. On `sm_6x` and earlier, all named lanes must execute in convergence and no unnamed lane may be active. Both immediate and register member masks are admitted.

## Active-mask contract

- `active_mask` observes the lanes active at the instruction. LLVM uses the typed intrinsic; libNVVM uses reviewed convergent, side-effecting inline PTX because that backend does not select the intrinsic.

## Warp-match contracts

- `match_all_i64_sync` keeps operands in `[member_mask, value]` order and projects field 0 from LLVM's `{i32, i1}` result. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `match.sync` operation with the same qualifiers and mask. All register/immediate value and mask forms are admitted.
- `match_all_sync` keeps operands in `[member_mask, value]` order and projects field 0 from LLVM's `{i32, i1}` result. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `match.sync` operation with the same qualifiers and mask. All register/immediate value and mask forms are admitted.
- `match_any_i64_sync` keeps operands in `[member_mask, value]` order and returns LLVM's mask directly. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `match.sync` operation with the same qualifiers and mask. All register/immediate value and mask forms are admitted.
- `match_any_sync` keeps operands in `[member_mask, value]` order and returns LLVM's mask directly. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `match.sync` operation with the same qualifiers and mask. All register/immediate value and mask forms are admitted.

## Warp-barrier contract

- `sync_mask` passes the 32-bit member mask directly to the typed LLVM intrinsic on both backends. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `bar.warp.sync` operation with the same mask. On `sm_6x` and earlier, all named lanes must execute the barrier in convergence, and no unnamed lane may be active when it executes. The barrier orders memory accesses among participating lanes. Both immediate and register masks are admitted.

## Warp-shuffle contracts

- `shuffle_down_f32_sync` keeps raw and dialect operands in `[member_mask, value, lane_or_delta]` order and inserts clamp `31` during lowering. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `shfl.sync` operation with the same qualifiers and mask. On `sm_6x` and earlier, all named lanes must execute in convergence and no unnamed lane may be active. A computed in-range source must be active and named; if PTX marks it out of range, the calling lane's input is copied. Register and immediate lane/mask forms are admitted.
- `shuffle_down_sync` keeps raw and dialect operands in `[member_mask, value, lane_or_delta]` order and inserts clamp `31` during lowering. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `shfl.sync` operation with the same qualifiers and mask. On `sm_6x` and earlier, all named lanes must execute in convergence and no unnamed lane may be active. A computed in-range source must be active and named; if PTX marks it out of range, the calling lane's input is copied. Register and immediate lane/mask forms are admitted.
- `shuffle_down_u64_sync` keeps raw and dialect operands in `[member_mask, value, lane_or_delta]` order and inserts clamp `31` during lowering. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `shfl.sync` operation with the same qualifiers and mask. On `sm_6x` and earlier, all named lanes must execute in convergence and no unnamed lane may be active. A computed in-range source must be active and named; if PTX marks it out of range, the calling lane's input is copied. One convergent, side-effecting inline-PTX block splits `i64`, performs low then high `b32` shuffles with the same register lane/mask, and reassembles it.
- `shuffle_f32_sync` keeps raw and dialect operands in `[member_mask, value, lane_or_delta]` order and inserts clamp `31` during lowering. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `shfl.sync` operation with the same qualifiers and mask. On `sm_6x` and earlier, all named lanes must execute in convergence and no unnamed lane may be active. A computed in-range source must be active and named; if PTX marks it out of range, the calling lane's input is copied. Register and immediate lane/mask forms are admitted.
- `shuffle_sync` keeps raw and dialect operands in `[member_mask, value, lane_or_delta]` order and inserts clamp `31` during lowering. The executing lane must be named in the mask, and every non-exited named lane must execute the same `shfl.sync` operation with the same qualifiers and mask. On `sm_6x` and earlier, all named lanes must execute in convergence and no unnamed lane may be active. One convergent, side-effecting inline-PTX block splits `i64`, performs low then high `b32` shuffles with the same register lane/mask, and reassembles it.

## CTA synchronization contracts

- `sync_threads` inserts the fixed barrier ID `0`. Every active CTA thread must reach the same barrier; divergent use can deadlock the CTA.

## cp.async mbarrier contracts

- `cp_async_mbarrier_arrive` uses generic addressing and increments the pending count before the later asynchronous decrement. It associates only the executing thread's prior `cp.async` operations with a live, eight-byte-aligned shared-memory barrier. LLVM-NVPTX uses the typed intrinsic; libNVVM uses reviewed convergent, side-effecting inline PTX with a memory clobber.
- `cp_async_mbarrier_arrive_noinc` uses generic addressing and does not increment the pending count, so initialization must already include the later asynchronous decrement. It associates only the executing thread's prior `cp.async` operations with a live, eight-byte-aligned shared-memory barrier. LLVM-NVPTX uses the typed intrinsic; libNVVM uses reviewed convergent, side-effecting inline PTX with a memory clobber.
- `cp_async_mbarrier_arrive_noinc_shared` uses explicit shared addressing and does not increment the pending count, so initialization must already include the later asynchronous decrement. It associates only the executing thread's prior `cp.async` operations with a live, eight-byte-aligned shared-memory barrier. LLVM-NVPTX uses the typed intrinsic; libNVVM uses reviewed convergent, side-effecting inline PTX with a memory clobber.
- `cp_async_mbarrier_arrive_shared` uses explicit shared addressing and increments the pending count before the later asynchronous decrement. It associates only the executing thread's prior `cp.async` operations with a live, eight-byte-aligned shared-memory barrier. LLVM-NVPTX uses the typed intrinsic; libNVVM uses reviewed convergent, side-effecting inline PTX with a memory clobber.

## Basic mbarrier contracts

- `mbarrier_arrive` records one expected arrival and returns a token for the same barrier phase. It lowers through the typed NVVM intrinsic with LLVM-NVPTX and inline PTX with libNVVM; generic MIR pointers are normalized to shared address space during lowering.
- `mbarrier_init` initializes one eight-byte-aligned shared-memory object exactly once with an expected count in `1..=0xFFFFF`. It lowers through the typed NVVM intrinsic with LLVM-NVPTX and inline PTX with libNVVM; generic MIR pointers are normalized to shared address space during lowering.
- `mbarrier_inval` invalidates an initialized barrier only after all users are finished. It lowers through the typed NVVM intrinsic with LLVM-NVPTX and inline PTX with libNVVM; generic MIR pointers are normalized to shared address space during lowering.
- `mbarrier_test_wait` tests one token from the same barrier phase with convergent, side-effecting inline PTX. It lowers through inline PTX on both backends; generic MIR pointers are normalized to shared address space during lowering.
